## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus Metrics Exposition Pattern Across Kubernetes and Grafana

## Your Task

Find the Go source files in both kubernetes/kubernetes and grafana/grafana that implement the Prometheus metrics exposition pattern: where metrics are registered using the Prometheus client_golang library, how metric collectors are organized, and where the `/metrics` HTTP endpoint is configured to expose them. Compare how both projects structure their metrics infrastructure.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain. Both Kubernetes and Grafana use the Prometheus client_golang library to expose internal metrics, but they organize their metrics registration and exposition differently. Your goal is to map these patterns across both codebases.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?
- **Symbol identification**: Correct symbol names and locations?
- **Keyword presence**: Did you mention key concepts (metrics registry, collectors, exposition)?

## Kubernetes (`sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`)

Infrastructure** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/`)\\n\\nKubernetes builds a custom metrics stability framework on top of `prometheus/client_golang`. The core is in:\\n\\n- `registry.go`: Defines the `KubeRegistry` interface and `kubeRegistry` struct. The `kubeRegistry` wraps a `prometheus.Registry` (via the `PromRegistry` interface defined in `wrappers.go`) and adds Kubernetes-specific features: metric versioning/deprecation lifecycle, hidden metric management, and resettable metrics. Key symbols: `NewKubeRegistry`, `Registerable` (interface that all k8s metrics must implement, extending `prometheus.Collector`), `KubeRegistry` (interface with `Register`, `MustRegister`, `CustomRegister`, `CustomMustRegister`, `RawMustRegister`), `RegisterMetaMetrics` (registers meta-metrics like `registered_metrics_total`, `disabled_metrics_total`, `hidden_metrics_total`).\\n\\n- `legacyregistry/registry.go`: Provides the **global singleton registry** used by almost all Kubernetes components. Key globals: `defaultRegistry` (a `KubeRegistry` created at package init), `DefaultGatherer`, `MustRegister`, `Register`, `RawMustRegister`, `CustomRegister`, `CustomMustRegister`. The `Handler()` function creates an HTTP handler using `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler` + `promhttp.HandlerFor(defaultRegistry, ...)`, and `HandlerWithReset()` supports DELETE-triggered resets. In `init()`, the process collector, Go runtime collector, and meta-metrics are registered.\\n\\n- `wrappers.go`: Defines reusable interfaces (`Collector`, `Metric`, `CounterMetric`, `GaugeMetric`, `Registerer`, `PromRegistry`) that wrap prometheus types to prevent upstream API breakage.\\n\\n**HTTP Endpoint Registration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/metrics.go`)\\n\\nThe `DefaultMetrics` struct (with `Install(*mux.PathRecorderMux)`) mounts `legacyregistry.Handler()` at `/metrics`. `MetricsWithReset` mounts `legacyregistry.HandlerWithReset()` at `/metrics`. The `register()` helper registers sub-system metrics (apiserver, cacher, etcd3, flowcontrol, peerproxy, handlers metrics) into the legacy registry.\\n\\n**SLI Metrics** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/slis/routes.go`)\\n\\n`SLIMetrics` and `SLIMetricsWithReset` install a separate `/metrics/slis` endpoint using a dedicated `Registry` (separate from the default), demonstrating Kubernetes's multi-registry pattern.\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**: Kubernetes components typically call `legacyregistry.MustRegister(metric)` from package-level `init()` functions (e.g., all etcd vendor metrics), or call a `Register()` function that wraps `legacyregistry.Register`. The stability framework intercepts registration to check if a metric is deprecated/hidden for the current Kubernetes version.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Grafana\\n\\n**Registry Infrastructure** (`pkg/infra/metrics/`)\\n\\nGrafana uses `prometheus/client_golang` more directly, with a dependency injection pattern via Wire:\\n\\n- `metrics.go`: Defines all global metric variables (counters, gauges, summaries, histograms) with package-level `var` declarations, initialized in `init()` using standard prometheus constructors (`prometheus.NewCounter`, `prometheus.NewGaugeVec`, etc.). All metrics use `ExporterName = \\\"grafana\\\"` as namespace. The `initMetricVars(reg prometheus.Registerer)` function calls `reg.MustRegister(...)` with all defined metrics. `SetBuildInformation` and `SetEnvironmentInformation` are utility functions that create and register ephemeral metrics.\\n\\n- `service.go`: Central service providing the DI wiring. `ProvideService(cfg, reg)` calls `initMetricVars(reg)` and `initFrontendMetrics(reg)` to register all metrics. `ProvideRegisterer()` returns `legacyregistry.Registerer()` (Kubernetes's legacy registry is reused as the global registerer). `ProvideGatherer()` creates a `multiRegistry` combining an `addPrefixWrapper` (which prefixes non-`grafana_`/`go_` k8s metrics with `grafana_`) around the k8s legacy registry gatherer, plus `prometheus.DefaultGatherer`. This unified gatherer is what gets exposed at `/metrics`.\\n\\n- `frontendmetrics.go`: `initFrontendMetrics(r)` registers histogram metrics for frontend performance timings using `registerFrontendHistogram`.\\n\\n- `settings.go`: Handles optional Graphite bridge configuration for pushing metrics to Graphite via `graphitebridge.NewBridge`.\\n\\n- `wireset.go`: Wire dependency injection set: `WireSet` exposes `ProvideService`, `ProvideRegisterer`, `ProvideGatherer`.\\n\\n- `metricutil/utils.go`: Helpers `NewCounterStartingAtZero` and `NewCounterVecStartingAtZero` initialize counters pre-seeded at zero for label consistency.\\n\\n**HTTP Endpoint** (`pkg/api/http_server.go`)\\n\\nThe `HTTPServer.metricsEndpoint` method (registered as a web middleware via `m.Use(hs.metricsEndpoint)`) handles `GET /metrics`. It checks `hs.Cfg.MetricsEndpointEnabled`, optionally enforces HTTP basic auth, and then calls `promhttp.HandlerFor(hs.promGatherer, promhttp.HandlerOpts{EnableOpenMetrics: true}).ServeHTTP(...)`. The `promGatherer` is the `multiRegistry` provided by `ProvideGatherer()`. The `HTTPServer` also holds a `promRegister` (used by `middleware.RequestMetrics` for HTTP request instrumentation).\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Registry abstraction**: Kubernetes wraps prometheus in a full `KubeRegistry` abstraction with versioning/deprecation lifecycle management; Grafana uses prometheus types directly.\\n\\n2. **Global vs. DI**: Kubernetes uses a global package-level `defaultRegistry` in `legacyregistry`; Grafana uses Wire dependency injection to pass `prometheus.Registerer` and `prometheus.Gatherer` through the service graph.\\n\\n3. **Multi-gatherer**: Grafana's `ProvideGatherer()` builds a `multiRegistry` that merges the Kubernetes legacy registry (with a `grafana_` prefix wrapper) and the prometheus default registry\u2014enabling it to expose both Grafana-specific and runtime metrics from a unified `/metrics` endpoint.\\n\\n4. **Endpoint mounting**: Kubernetes mounts `/metrics` via an `Install()` method on a `PathRecorderMux` (declarative route registration); Grafana handles it as a low-level web middleware that intercepts matching requests before routing.\\n\\n5. **Metric collectors**: Kubernetes uses `StableCollector` (a custom interface for complex collectors with hidden/deprecated metric support via `CustomRegister`/`CustomMustRegister`); Grafana uses standard `prometheus.Collector` implementations.\"\n}\n",

(sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0)\\n\\n**Registry Infrastructure** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/`)\\n\\nKubernetes builds a custom metrics stability framework on top of `prometheus/client_golang`. The core is in:\\n\\n- `registry.go`: Defines the `KubeRegistry` interface and `kubeRegistry` struct. The `kubeRegistry` wraps a `PromRegistry` (defined in `wrappers.go` as a subset of `prometheus.Registerer`+`prometheus.Gatherer`) and adds Kubernetes-specific features: metric versioning/deprecation lifecycle, hidden metric management, and resettable metrics. Key symbols: `NewKubeRegistry` (creates a new registry backed by `prometheus.NewRegistry()`), `Registerable` (interface that all k8s metrics must implement, extending `prometheus.Collector` with `Create`, `ClearState`, `FQName`), `KubeRegistry` (interface with `Register`, `MustRegister`, `CustomRegister`, `CustomMustRegister`, `RawMustRegister`), `RegisterMetaMetrics` (registers meta-metrics: `registered_metrics_total`, `disabled_metrics_total`, `hidden_metrics_total`, `cardinality_enforcement_unexpected_categorizations_total`).\\n\\n- `legacyregistry/registry.go`: Provides the **global singleton registry** used by almost all Kubernetes components. Key globals: `defaultRegistry` (a `KubeRegistry` created at package init via `metrics.NewKubeRegistry()`), `DefaultGatherer`, `MustRegister`, `Register`, `RawMustRegister`, `CustomRegister`, `CustomMustRegister`. The `Handler()` function creates an HTTP handler using `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler` + `promhttp.HandlerFor(defaultRegistry, promhttp.HandlerOpts{ProcessStartTime: processStart})`. `HandlerWithReset()` wraps a handler that also supports DELETE-triggered registry resets. In `init()`, the process collector, Go runtime collector (with all runtime metrics), and meta-metrics are registered via `RawMustRegister` and `RegisterMetaMetrics`.\\n\\n- `wrappers.go`: Defines reusable interfaces (`Collector`, `Metric`, `CounterMetric`, `GaugeMetric`, `Registerer`, `PromRegistry`) that wrap prometheus types for API stability.\\n\\n**HTTP Endpoint Registration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/metrics.go`)\\n\\nThe `DefaultMetrics` struct (with `Install(*mux.PathRecorderMux)`) mounts `legacyregistry.Handler()` at `/metrics`. `MetricsWithReset` mounts `legacyregistry.HandlerWithReset()` at `/metrics`. The `register()` helper registers apiserver, cacher, etcd3, flowcontrol, peerproxy, and handlers metrics into the legacy registry before mounting.\\n\\n**SLI Metrics** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/slis/routes.go`)\\n\\n`SLIMetrics` and `SLIMetricsWithReset` install a separate `/metrics/slis` endpoint using a dedicated `Registry` (separate from the default), demonstrating Kubernetes's multi-endpoint pattern.\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**: Kubernetes components call `legacyregistry.MustRegister(metric)` from package-level `init()` functions, or call a `Register()` function that wraps `legacyregistry.Register`. The stability framework intercepts registration to check if a metric is deprecated/hidden for the current Kubernetes version, hiding it if appropriate.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Grafana (sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0)\\n\\n**Registry Infrastructure** (`pkg/infra/metrics/`)\\n\\nGrafana uses `prometheus/client_golang` more directly, with a Wire dependency injection pattern:\\n\\n- `metrics.go`: Defines all global metric variables (counters, gauges, summaries, histograms) as package-level `var` declarations, all initialized in `init()` using standard prometheus constructors (`prometheus.NewCounter`, `prometheus.NewGaugeVec`, `prometheus.NewSummary`, `prometheus.NewHistogram`, etc.). All metrics use `ExporterName = \\\"grafana\\\"` as namespace. The `initMetricVars(reg prometheus.Registerer)` function bulk-registers all metrics via `reg.MustRegister(...)`. `SetBuildInformation` and `SetEnvironmentInformation` create and register additional labeled gauge metrics at runtime.\\n\\n- `service.go`: The central DI-wired service. `ProvideService(cfg, reg)` calls `initMetricVars(reg)` and `initFrontendMetrics(reg)` to register all metrics. `ProvideRegisterer()` returns `legacyregistry.Registerer()` (Kubernetes's k8s.io/component-base legacy registry is reused as the global registerer, allowing Kubernetes runtime metrics to also appear). `ProvideGatherer()` creates a `multiRegistry` combining an `addPrefixWrapper` (which prefixes non-`grafana_`/`go_` k8s metrics with `grafana_`) around the k8s legacy registry gatherer, plus `prometheus.DefaultGatherer`. This unified multi-gatherer is what gets exposed at `/metrics`.\\n\\n- `frontendmetrics.go`: `initFrontendMetrics(r)` registers histogram metrics for frontend performance timings (boot time, first paint, JS/CSS load) via `registerFrontendHistogram`.\\n\\n- `settings.go`: Handles optional Graphite bridge configuration for pushing metrics to Graphite via `graphitebridge.NewBridge`.\\n\\n- `wireset.go`: Wire DI set exporting `ProvideService`, `ProvideRegisterer`, `ProvideGatherer`.\\n\\n- `metricutil/utils.go`: Helpers `NewCounterStartingAtZero` and `NewCounterVecStartingAtZero` initialize counters pre-seeded at zero for label consistency across label value sets.\\n\\n**HTTP Endpoint** (`pkg/api/http_server.go`)\\n\\nThe `HTTPServer.metricsEndpoint` method (registered as a web middleware at line 637 via `m.Use(hs.metricsEndpoint)`) handles `GET /metrics`. It checks `hs.Cfg.MetricsEndpointEnabled`, optionally enforces HTTP basic auth, then calls `promhttp.HandlerFor(hs.promGatherer, promhttp.HandlerOpts{EnableOpenMetrics: true}).ServeHTTP(...)`. The `promGatherer` is the `multiRegistry` from `ProvideGatherer()`. The `HTTPServer` also holds `promRegister` used by `middleware.RequestMetrics` for per-request HTTP instrumentation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Registry abstraction**: Kubernetes wraps prometheus in a `KubeRegistry` abstraction with versioning/deprecation lifecycle management; Grafana uses prometheus types directly.\\n\\n2. **Global vs. DI**: Kubernetes uses a global package-level `defaultRegistry` in `legacyregistry`; Grafana uses Wire DI to pass `prometheus.Registerer` and `prometheus.Gatherer` through the service graph.\\n\\n3. **Multi-gatherer**: Grafana's `ProvideGatherer()` builds a `multiRegistry` merging the Kubernetes legacy registry (with a `grafana_` prefix wrapper for non-prefixed metrics) and `prometheus.DefaultGatherer`\u2014enabling a unified `/metrics` exposition from both registries.\\n\\n4. **Endpoint mounting**: Kubernetes mounts `/metrics` via an explicit `Install()` method on `PathRecorderMux` (declarative); Grafana handles it as a low-level web middleware intercepting matching requests.\\n\\n5. **Collector registration**: Kubernetes uses `StableCollector` for complex collectors with hidden/deprecated metric support via `CustomRegister`/`CustomMustRegister`; Grafana uses standard `prometheus.Collector` implementations with a helper utility (`metricutil`) for zero-seeded counters.\"\n}\n",

The `initMetricVars(reg prometheus.Registerer)` function bulk-registers all metrics via `reg.MustRegister(...)`. `SetBuildInformation` and `SetEnvironmentInformation` create and register additional labeled gauge metrics at runtime.\\n\\n- `service.go`: The central DI-wired service. `ProvideService(cfg, reg)` calls `initMetricVars(reg)` and `initFrontendMetrics(reg)` to register all metrics. `ProvideRegisterer()` returns `legacyregistry.Registerer()` (Kubernetes's k8s.io/component-base legacy registry is reused as the global registerer, allowing Kubernetes runtime metrics to also appear). `ProvideGatherer()` creates a `multiRegistry` combining an `addPrefixWrapper` (which prefixes non-`grafana_`/`go_` k8s metrics with `grafana_`) around the k8s legacy registry gatherer, plus `prometheus.DefaultGatherer`. This unified multi-gatherer is what gets exposed at `/metrics`.\\n\\n- `frontendmetrics.go`: `initFrontendMetrics(r)` registers histogram metrics for frontend performance timings (boot time, first paint, JS/CSS load) via `registerFrontendHistogram`.\\n\\n- `settings.go`: Handles optional Graphite bridge configuration for pushing metrics to Graphite via `graphitebridge.NewBridge`.\\n\\n- `wireset.go`: Wire DI set exporting `ProvideService`, `ProvideRegisterer`, `ProvideGatherer`.\\n\\n- `metricutil/utils.go`: Helpers `NewCounterStartingAtZero` and `NewCounterVecStartingAtZero` initialize counters pre-seeded at zero for label consistency across label value sets.\\n\\n**HTTP Endpoint** (`pkg/api/http_server.go`)\\n\\nThe `HTTPServer.metricsEndpoint` method (registered as a web middleware at line 637 via `m.Use(hs.metricsEndpoint)`) handles `GET /metrics`. It checks `hs.Cfg.MetricsEndpointEnabled`, optionally enforces HTTP basic auth, then calls `promhttp.HandlerFor(hs.promGatherer, promhttp.HandlerOpts{EnableOpenMetrics: true}).ServeHTTP(...)`. The `promGatherer` is the `multiRegistry` from `ProvideGatherer()`. The `HTTPServer` also holds `promRegister` used by `middleware.RequestMetrics` for per-request HTTP instrumentation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Registry abstraction**: Kubernetes wraps prometheus in a `KubeRegistry` abstraction with versioning/deprecation lifecycle management; Grafana uses prometheus types directly.\\n\\n2. **Global vs. DI**: Kubernetes uses a global package-level `defaultRegistry` in `legacyregistry`; Grafana uses Wire DI to pass `prometheus.Registerer` and `prometheus.Gatherer` through the service graph.\\n\\n3. **Multi-gatherer**: Grafana's `ProvideGatherer()` builds a `multiRegistry` merging the Kubernetes legacy registry (with a `grafana_` prefix wrapper for non-prefixed metrics) and `prometheus.DefaultGatherer`\u2014enabling a unified `/metrics` exposition from both registries.\\n\\n4. **Endpoint mounting**: Kubernetes mounts `/metrics` via an explicit `Install()` method on `PathRecorderMux` (declarative); Grafana handles it as a low-level web middleware intercepting matching requests.\\n\\n5. **Collector registration**: Kubernetes uses `StableCollector` for complex collectors with hidden/deprecated metric support via `CustomRegister`/`CustomMustRegister`; Grafana uses standard `prometheus.Collector` implementations with a helper utility (`metricutil`) for zero-seeded counters.\"\n}\n",
